## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, which is fundamental to constitutive modeling in materials science. Temperature typically causes thermal softening (reducing elastic modulus and flow stress), while strain hardening increases stress with deformation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * epsilon)**c3 (nonlinear stress-strain)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T**c3) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook homologous form: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (thermal softening with melting reference)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with temperature effect)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation combined with hardening)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal effect)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Zerilli-Armstrong BCC model: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp((c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**c4) (dislocation mechanics based constitutive model)
- Linear modulus with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of elastic modulus)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening typically appears as multiplicative factor (1 - (T/Tm)^n) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening in metals follows power-law epsilon^n with n typically between 0.1 and 0.5
- Combined thermo-mechanical effects are usually multiplicative (separable): sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T)
- Yield stress offset suggests additive constant: sigma = sigma_y + f(epsilon) where sigma_y may depend on T
- Saturating hardening (Voce-type) uses exponential approach: sigma ~ c*(1 - exp(-k*epsilon))
- Phase transitions or material instabilities may introduce non-monotonic temperature dependence
- At very small strains, stress-strain should be approximately linear (tangent modulus regime)
- Dislocation-based models often combine sqrt(epsilon) or epsilon^0.5 terms with Boltzmann thermal factors

This has terms: `epsilon**2`, `T*epsilon`, `epsilon`, `T*log(epsilon+1)`, `log(epsilon+1)`

**Candidate 27:** `T*c0*epsilon**2 + c1 + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon*log(c5*epsilon + 1)`

**Candidate 30:** `T*c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c1 + c3*(c4 + epsilon)**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7`

No log terms at all. No match.

**Candidate 15:** `T*c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c1 + c3*exp(c4*epsilon**c5) + c6*exp(T*c7) + c8*epsilon + c9`

Has exp(T*c7) which can't produce T*log(epsilon+1). No match.

**Candidate 25:** `T*c0*epsilon/(T*c1+1) + T*c2*sin(c3+c4*log(c5*epsilon+1))/(T*c1+1) + c6*epsilon/(T*c1+1) + c7*sin(...)/(T*c1+1) + c8/(T*c1+1)`
